<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7963972324833835772">All those who enjoyed shuddering their way through Alvin Schwartz's first volume of Scary Stories To Tell In The Dark will find a satisfyingly spooky sequel in this new collection of the macabre, the funny, and the fantastic.Is it possible to die -- and not know it? What if a person is buried too soon? What happens to a thief foolish enough to rob a corpse, or to a murdere</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7963972324833835772">All those who enjoyed shuddering their way through Alvin Schwartz's first volume of Scary Stories To Tell In The Dark will find a satisfyingly spooky sequel in this new collection of the macabre, the funny, and the fantastic.Is it possible to die -- and not know it? What if a person is buried too soon? What happens to a thief foolish enough to rob a corpse, or to a murderer whose victim returns from the grave? Read about these terrifying predicaments as well as what happens when practical jokes produce gruesome consequences and initiations go awry.Stephen Gammell's splendidly creepy drawings perfectly capture the mood of more than two dozen scary stories -- and even a scary song -- all just right for reading alone or for telling aloud in the dark.If You Dare!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7963972324833835772">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_453213969">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/453213969" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell" class="left imgcol" title="Ronyell"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1423803024p2/1169488.jpg" alt="Ronyell" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/453213969?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 15, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell" class="user" title="Ronyell">Ronyell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/413110.More_Scary_Stories_to_Tell_in_the_Dark" title="Hardcover 9780397320820" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of dark and spooky stories!!!</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=fairy-tales-folktales" class="actionLinkLite">fairy-tales-folktales</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=creepy-ending" class="actionLinkLite">creepy-ending</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=banned-books" class="actionLinkLite">banned-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=alvin-schwartz" class="actionLinkLite">alvin-schwartz</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews" class="actionLinkLite">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=children-s-book" class="actionLinkLite">children-s-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer453213969">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15254487152495148811"><img width="300" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="Sausage" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397226i/766240.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong> <em>4.5 stars</em> </strong><br /><br /><strong> <u>SCARY STORIES PART TWO!</u> </strong><br /><br />After reading the first book “Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark,” I just had to read up on the sequel, “More Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark,” which is also written by Alvin Schwartz along with illustrations by Stephen Gammell. “More Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark” is a continuation of the first book and we are introduced to more spine-tingling tales from this fantastic series as you will definitely be sitting on the edge of your seats after you read this</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15254487152495148811"><img width="300" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="Sausage" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397226i/766240.jpg" /><br /><br /><strong>
  <em>4.5 stars</em>
</strong><br /><br /><strong>
  <u>SCARY STORIES PART TWO!</u>
</strong><br /><br />After reading the first book “Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark,” I just had to read up on the sequel, “More Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark,” which is also written by Alvin Schwartz along with illustrations by Stephen Gammell. “More Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark” is a continuation of the first book and we are introduced to more spine-tingling tales from this fantastic series as you will definitely be sitting on the edge of your seats after you read this collection of scary stories!<br /><br />Just like the first book, this book basically contains a collection of scary stories to tell in the dark and they include:<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>One Sunday Morning</u>
</strong><br /><br /><img width="300" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="Sunday Morning" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397226i/766241.jpg" /><br /><br />A young woman named Ida decided to go to church on Sunday morning and when she made it to the church, she started to realize that the people at the church were not normal as she saw one of her friends, Josephine Kerr, attend the service, even though she died a month ago…<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>The Little Black Dog</u>
</strong><br /><br /><img width="300" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="Little Black Dog" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397226i/766242.jpg" /><br /><br />Billy Mansfield was fighting a man named Silas Burton, who was an enemy of his family and when Billy knocked Silas off his horse, he ended up killing Silas along with his black dog when the dog started barking at Billy. Unfortunately after that incident, Billy starts noticing a strange black dog following him around…<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>The Bride</u>
</strong><br /><br /><img width="300" height="300" class="escapedImg" alt="the Bride" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397226i/766243.jpg" /><br /><br />A minister’s daughter just got married and after the wedding ceremony, she decided to play hide and seek and she hid inside a trunk in the attic. Unfortunately, the lid of the trunk dropped on the daughter and locked her inside the trunk and everyone at the wedding ceremony did not even know that she is missing!<br /><br />Once again, I was blown away by this collection of scary stories from the creative retellings of Alvin Schwartz! Alvin Schwartz has done a brilliant job at retelling these ancient scary folktales as each story is just as creepy and intense as the last story and the twist endings are enough to make you scream! I loved the way that Alvin Schwartz provided an eerie atmosphere to each story as it makes the audience feel scare for the characters and the supernatural activities that surround them and it really brought out the creativity of this book. I also loved the fact that Alvin Schwartz took the time to research the various folktales dealing with horror and I loved the fact that Alvin Schwartz provided a bibliography section at the end of the book so that way you would be able to go back and check the original sources of these tales! I enjoyed most of the stories in this collection, but my most favorite stories would have to be “The Bride,” “The Little Black Dog,” “One Sunday Morning,” “Wonderful Sausage” and “The Cat in a Shopping Bag.” Stephen Gammell’s illustrations are as usual, eerily and brilliantly done as the artwork is truly frightening to look at and the black and white colorings of the illustrations really bring out the creepy feel to the stories. There is much creepy imagery in this book, but probably the scariest image in this book was of the skeletal bride in “The Bride.” <br /><br />Just like the first book, this book might be too scary for small children since there are stories about characters being killed and haunted by supernatural forces. Also, what always made this series so scary for small children is the fact that the illustrations are truly scary and small children might not be able to get through this book because of the scary illustration. As for why I took off half a point from the rating, I felt that this book was using the same structure that was used in the first book such as in stories like “Cemetery Soup” where the character always steal something from the dead and something haunts them at the end.<br /><br />Overall, “More Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark” is just another addition to your “Horror Books for Children” shelf that you just got to check out! I would recommend this book to children ages eight and up since the often spooky content in this book is too scary for small children.<br /><br /><strong>Review is also on: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/11/more-scary-stories-to-tell-in-dark-by.html">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></strong></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15254487152495148811">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_331477341">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331477341" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2853899-megan" class="left imgcol" title="Megan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1365634450p2/2853899.jpg" alt="Megan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/331477341?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 17, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2853899-megan" class="user" title="Megan">Megan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/150859.More_Scary_Stories_to_Tell_in_the_Dark" title="Paperback 9780440842651" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2853899-megan?shelf=kyle-s-books" class="actionLinkLite">kyle-s-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2853899-megan?shelf=owned" class="actionLinkLite">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer331477341">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3933902165966815940">When I was a child, I used to love reading Alvin Schwartz's scary story books! There was nothing more fun than going to the library during the summer and getting my fix of creepy stories and macabre artwork by Stephen Gammell. I recently picked up a copy of this book as a testament to my childhood nostalgia to see if the stories held up to the test of time. I'm glad to say that they did! While written for children, the stories definitely gave me a few chills as an adult. The artwork is still jus</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3933902165966815940">When I was a child, I used to love reading Alvin Schwartz's scary story books! There was nothing more fun than going to the library during the summer and getting my fix of creepy stories and macabre artwork by Stephen Gammell. I recently picked up a copy of this book as a testament to my childhood nostalgia to see if the stories held up to the test of time. I'm glad to say that they did! While written for children, the stories definitely gave me a few chills as an adult. The artwork is still just as creepy, although I'm not quite as scared to look at it now. The tales are based on folklore and legends, so you or your children may have already heard many of them before. Yet, there is nothing quite like the way that Alvin Schwartz tells them.<br /><br />This is definitely a book I'd recommend picking up for children who love scary stories, or for those of us who loved these stories as a child! Don't forget to read them when the sun is out and the lights are on, though. Otherwise, you might start seeing things in every corner or hearing things in every room!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3933902165966815940">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1183649186100380690">I still love these books. They're still pretty spooky, because the stories are archetypal. Some things are always scary. For the target audience, this will likely be their first exposure to most of these archetypes. And nostalgia helps those of us who read these years ago.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText1183649186100380690">I still love these books. They're still pretty spooky, because the stories are archetypal. Some things are always scary. For the target audience, this will likely be their first exposure to most of these archetypes. And nostalgia helps those of us who read these years ago. The stories are nice and short, perfect for telling around a campfire or at a sleepover.<br /><br />The original art by Stephen Gammell is horrible and I love it. I always did. It was a pleasure to be horrified by it. The newest edition has replaced the art with art by Brett Helquist, which is creepy but not nearly as nightmare inducing as the original. Sigh.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/12743390-kelsey-trinkner" class="user" title="Kelsey Trinkner">Kelsey Trinkner</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/413110.More_Scary_Stories_to_Tell_in_the_Dark" title="Hardcover 9780397320820" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/12743390-kelsey-trinkner?shelf=read-junior-year" class="actionLinkLite">read-junior-year</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer617141691">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7030435628692400178">When I was little, my mother bought me this series of books. I read all of them within a short period of time. I loved the books. I used to loan them out to my classmates when I was in the third grade. I would also read these stories to my little brother. They scared him, but I loved them. I recently re-read these three books. My favorite story from this book is called "The Bed By The Window." This story is about a few men who are in a nursing home. The three men are unable to lift themselves ou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7030435628692400178">When I was little, my mother bought me this series of books. I read all of them within a short period of time. I loved the books. I used to loan them out to my classmates when I was in the third grade. I would also read these stories to my little brother. They scared him, but I loved them. I recently re-read these three books. My favorite story from this book is called "The Bed By The Window." This story is about a few men who are in a nursing home. The three men are unable to lift themselves out of their beds and walk around. In the room Ted, George and Richard share, there is only one window. Ted's bed was next to the window, until he died. George took Ted's bed while Richard took George's bed. George would always describe in detail to Richard what he saw outside the window. He saw pretty girls, policemen on horseback, traffic jams and other such scenes. Richard became jealous of George and eventually killed him by hiding his pills. He then took over his bed and was heartbroken when he looked out the window only to see a blank brick wall. I will continue to read these stories in the future and I would love to share them with anyone and everyone.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7030435628692400178">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer268780439">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3384163853041157641">I loved scary stories as a kid. I also was a dork, and loved to write. I entered some kind of "kid author/illustrator" contest in 4th or 5th grade, and I won! I remember that the highlight of winning included meeting awesome author Gary Paulsen and illustrator Stephen Gammell. Stephen Gammell, in my memory, was super amazing, and even created a creepy watercolor painting during the seminar. I also happened to love Alvin Schwartz's book <u> In a Dark, Dark Room and Other Scary Stories </u>, who also wro</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3384163853041157641">I loved scary stories as a kid. I also was a dork, and loved to write. I entered some kind of "kid author/illustrator" contest in 4th or 5th grade, and I won! I remember that the highlight of winning included meeting awesome author Gary Paulsen and illustrator Stephen Gammell. Stephen Gammell, in my memory, was super amazing, and even created a creepy watercolor painting during the seminar. I also happened to love Alvin Schwartz's book <u> In a Dark, Dark Room and Other Scary Stories </u>, who also wrote this book! Imagine my surprise, years later, to discover that my boyfriend and I both read these books, and were sort of obsessed with them. "The Girl with the Yellow Ribbon" still haunts my memory, in a good way. I love these scary Americana folk tale stories, and am crazy for the watercolor or pen &amp; ink drawings by Gammell. Amazing! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3384163853041157641">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8673430793424317807">My sister and I loved these when we were little - the stories were generic urban myths but it was the disturbing and eerie illustrations that made this anthology series so memorable, the stark black and white with hints of bright red and blue to evoke the chilling atmosphere.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer58739455">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5231309700361382565"> As in the first volume, the storytelling skills of Alvin Schwartz and the eerie drawings of the more than capable Stephen Gammell come together in the telling of these incredibly scary folk tales.<br /> For some reason, "Wonderful Sausage" has always caught my fascination, though the story itself is chillingly brutal. "Oh, Susannah" has always been one of the scariest stories of any in the Alvin Schwartz collections that I have read, and more than once I found myself truly getting cold with goosebump</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5231309700361382565"> As in the first volume, the storytelling skills of Alvin Schwartz and the eerie drawings of the more than capable Stephen Gammell come together in the telling of these incredibly scary folk tales.<br /> For some reason, "Wonderful Sausage" has always caught my fascination, though the story itself is chillingly brutal. "Oh, Susannah" has always been one of the scariest stories of any in the Alvin Schwartz collections that I have read, and more than once I found myself truly getting cold with goosebumps as I read through this collection.<br /> Meticulously researched, well told, and one of the scariest books of its type out there, "More Scary Stories To Tell in the Dark" is an exceptional book. </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16713812388268334410">Horror stories are always and will always be part of anyone ones child hood. This book written by Mr.Alvin Schwartz has been part of my childhood. I remember first reading this book, when I was in elementary school. But it wasn't just the writing that spooked me, but the illustrations. And I know I wasn't just the only kid who grew up and still remembers this book and the other two books in the series. More Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark, along with the other two, are a great read for old, young, and those in between. They make a great read at camping trips, sleep overs, and even just to sit down and read. I really recommend this book. Especially if you like scary stories. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/455001414?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 06, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12737746-trevor-fitzpatrick" class="user" title="Trevor Fitzpatrick">Trevor Fitzpatrick</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/413110.More_Scary_Stories_to_Tell_in_the_Dark" title="Hardcover 9780397320820" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer455001414">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16065410800328823332">As a kid I remembered reading the first book of this series and of course all of the stories scarred me at night. I never read the second book out of the series though, which is this book, and I personally enjoyed it a lot. The style of the book was the same old one to four page scary story and some of them were actually pretty good; even reading them now. Whether it be a sausage maker grinding people up into sausage, or demonic people falling from the sky to haunt a ship, each story had its own</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16065410800328823332">As a kid I remembered reading the first book of this series and of course all of the stories scarred me at night. I never read the second book out of the series though, which is this book, and I personally enjoyed it a lot. The style of the book was the same old one to four page scary story and some of them were actually pretty good; even reading them now. Whether it be a sausage maker grinding people up into sausage, or demonic people falling from the sky to haunt a ship, each story had its own unique style. My personal favorite is the ghost story called "The Window" which is about a vampire that breaks into this girl's house and bites her neck and gets away with it. I would recommend this book to anyone who likes a good scare, or someone who just likes creepy things in general. I would not recommend this book to children under 12 though because some of the stories pretty creepy. This book was very entertaining and I actually looked forward to reading it during silent reading.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16065410800328823332">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/20642273-mikal-o-boyle" class="user" title="Mikal O'Boyle">Mikal O'Boyle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/120876.More_Scary_Stories_to_Tell_in_the_Dark" title="Paperback 9780590135863" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1010065108">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15609239213227686602">Alvin Schwartz is a great storyteller who has teamed up with a very talented, and possibly demented, illustrator named Stephen Gammell. I found this book, More Scary Stories, (appropriately so) in the attic and instantly remembered a handful of tales that thrilled me as a child. These stories, along with their grotesque illustrations, are dark and chilling. They are perfect for when that Halloween mood hits, and you're feeling mysterious and terrifying. They are gems of haunting stories and song</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15609239213227686602">Alvin Schwartz is a great storyteller who has teamed up with a very talented, and possibly demented, illustrator named Stephen Gammell. I found this book, More Scary Stories, (appropriately so) in the attic and instantly remembered a handful of tales that thrilled me as a child. These stories, along with their grotesque illustrations, are dark and chilling. They are perfect for when that Halloween mood hits, and you're feeling mysterious and terrifying. They are gems of haunting stories and songs that are easy to read and full of imagery. The best part is that they drastically vary from each other, pushing you from one frightening moment to another. Some are humorous to lighten up the mood while others are more scream-tastic. Think of it as a more disturbing version of Tim Burton. If you're looking for a bit of terror, then crack open this book!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15609239213227686602">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer469693446">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9176543184195509508">"More Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark" is a continuation to the book "Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark," and this book's contents are obvious by its name. The stories tell about a multitude of things, from ghosts to strange voices to people going crazy. There are plenty of stories in here to read. I didn't find these stories scary, but they would be great to read around a campfire, or to kids in the dark, as children would be scared by these and may find them enjoyable. I would recommend this</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9176543184195509508">"More Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark" is a continuation to the book "Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark," and this book's contents are obvious by its name. The stories tell about a multitude of things, from ghosts to strange voices to people going crazy. There are plenty of stories in here to read. I didn't find these stories scary, but they would be great to read around a campfire, or to kids in the dark, as children would be scared by these and may find them enjoyable. I would recommend this book only to kids, or adults if you plan on reading to kids. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1317344712">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1317344712" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/34627993-trevor" class="left imgcol" title="Trevor"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1419351960p2/34627993.jpg" alt="Trevor" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1317344712?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 25, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/34627993-trevor" class="user" title="Trevor">Trevor</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1317344712">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13738888608287590210">The book <em>More Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark</em> was an interesting series of short scary stories. It wasn’t that scary because I've read scarier stories. I only read the first five stories they were interesting and disturbing. It seems that the further you get into the book the scarier it gets. <br /><br />The plot for the first one was a ghost not knowing he was dead. He saw everyone around him run away not knowing what is going on he calls his wife his response was she was at his funeral. In the second st</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13738888608287590210">The book <em>More Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark</em> was an interesting series of short scary stories. It wasn’t that scary because I've read scarier stories. I only read the first five stories they were interesting and disturbing. It seems that the further you get into the book the scarier it gets.	<br /><br />The plot for the first one was a ghost not knowing he was dead. He saw everyone around him run away not knowing what is going on he calls his wife his response was she was at his funeral. In the second story there were two teens at a Christmas ball. They left to go to a movie one did not see the other so he went back only to see she had an accident. The third is a woman in church the only other people in the church were the undead. The fourth is about a sighting of a ghost ship. The fifth and final story I read was the only unnerving one it was about a ghost on a ship that took revenge against his killer.	<br /><br />The people I would recommend this too are campers who like to tell scary stories at night and people who just want a creepy book to pass the time. I recommend this to guys and girls that like dark books. The age group I would recommend this is young teen to young adult.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13738888608287590210">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_228553188">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228553188" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6279399-amy" class="left imgcol" title="Amy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1326734254p2/6279399.jpg" alt="Amy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/228553188?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 28, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6279399-amy" class="user" title="Amy">Amy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/413110.More_Scary_Stories_to_Tell_in_the_Dark" title="Hardcover 9780397320820" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6279399-amy?shelf=young-adult-lit" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6279399-amy?shelf=thriller-mystery" class="actionLinkLite">thriller-mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6279399-amy?shelf=children-s-lit" class="actionLinkLite">children-s-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer228553188">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13972086272685819688">I had to read this book for an assignment on "banned books" in a children's lit class. To save myself a trip to the library, I went to my (then) second grade daughter's and my (then) fourth grade daughter's classrooms and asked their teachers if they had "Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark" in their classroom collections. Both teachers said that they had had it in the past but that their copies had been "read to death" and they had not gotten around to replacing them. Fortunately, the literacy sp</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13972086272685819688">I had to read this book for an assignment on "banned books" in a children's lit class. To save myself a trip to the library, I went to my (then) second grade daughter's and my (then) fourth grade daughter's classrooms and asked their teachers if they had "Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark" in their classroom collections. Both teachers said that they had had it in the past but that their copies had been "read to death" and they had not gotten around to replacing them. Fortunately, the literacy specialist at my children's school had a copy of "More Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark" and she let me borrow it. She also commented that kids were CONSTANTLY checking these books out and that I was lucky to have come on a day when one was there.<br /><br />After reading it, I can certainly understand why parents would object to it. It's QUITE gruesome. I had to look at the copyright date (which is 1984) after I read "Wonderful Sausage". It was enough like the Jeffrey Dahmer story that I thought it might have been written AFTER that happened. It also reminded me a little of "The Silence of the Lambs". That said, I read several of the stories to my (then) 7 year old and my (then) 9 year old and they LOVED them. I couldn't believe it. I also remembered the thrill I used to get as a child when we would sit around the fire at girl-scout camp telling scary stories. For whatever reason, children ENJOY these creepy stories. Although I do NOT like them, I do not advocate banning them.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13972086272685819688">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer415548879">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12478527037224872804">This is a collection of strange, scary, shocking, gross and funny stories for older children. The tales presented are an interesting mix of old and new and our girls loved them. I was less enthused about the collection, although a good storyteller could have a lot of fun with these stories. <br /><br />The illustrations were scarier than the tales, in my opinion, but overall, it was an interesting compilation. We've also read <a title="Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark by Alvin Schwartz" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1325218.Scary_Stories_to_Tell_in_the_Dark">Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark</a> and will move on to <a title="Scary Stories 3 More Tales to Chill Your Bones by Alvin Schwartz" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/397150.Scary_Stories_3_More_Tales_to_Chill_Your_Bones">Scary Stories 3: More Tales</a></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12478527037224872804">This is a collection of strange, scary, shocking, gross and funny stories for older children. The tales presented are an interesting mix of old and new and our girls loved them. I was less enthused about the collection, although a good storyteller could have a lot of fun with these stories. <br /><br />The illustrations were scarier than the tales, in my opinion, but overall, it was an interesting compilation. We've also read <a title="Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark by Alvin Schwartz" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1325218.Scary_Stories_to_Tell_in_the_Dark">Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark</a> and will move on to <a title="Scary Stories 3 More Tales to Chill Your Bones by Alvin Schwartz" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/397150.Scary_Stories_3_More_Tales_to_Chill_Your_Bones">Scary Stories 3: More Tales to Chill Your Bones</a> next.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_482086905">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/482086905" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/12735275-aaron-ebert" class="left imgcol" title="Aaron_ebert"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Aaron_ebert" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/482086905?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 09, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12735275-aaron-ebert" class="user" title="Aaron_ebert">Aaron_ebert</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/413110.More_Scary_Stories_to_Tell_in_the_Dark" title="Hardcover 9780397320820" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">All Ages</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aaron_ebert by: </span>
      Lincoln VanCuick

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/12735275-aaron-ebert?shelf=scary" class="actionLinkLite">scary</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer482086905">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10799068015121988936">"More Scary Stories To Tell In The Dark" is a compilation of old folk tales and truly terrifying stories. My favorite story was about this person, described as a ticket, named McLaren from a ship called the Gertrude Spurshoe. They were sailing and a dead man fell from a loft. They couldn't figure out who it was. Guessing it was a stowaway. They wanted to throw the body overboard, but were afraid of a curse. McLaren states, "I've taken care of him once and I'll take care of him again." As McLaren</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10799068015121988936">"More Scary Stories To Tell In The Dark" is a compilation of old folk tales and truly terrifying stories. My favorite story was about this person, described as a ticket, named McLaren from a ship called the Gertrude Spurshoe. They were sailing and a dead man fell from a loft. They couldn't figure out who it was. Guessing it was a stowaway. They wanted to throw the body overboard, but were afraid of a curse. McLaren states, "I've taken care of him once and I'll take care of him again." As McLaren grabs the corpse, the dead corpse grabs back dragging both of them to the bottom of the ocean. McLaren was never seen again. This story was truly terrifying!!! This book would be perfect for anyone of any age interested in a good scare.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10799068015121988936">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/21555809-sparrow" class="user" title="Sparrow">Sparrow</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7952927-more-scary-stories-to-tell-in-the-dark" title="Paperback 9780060835224" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/21555809-sparrow?shelf=popsugar-challenge-2015" class="actionLinkLite">popsugar-challenge-2015</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21555809-sparrow?shelf=2015" class="actionLinkLite">2015</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1279573574">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8230014047221887199">Awesome when a book you read and reread as a child in the dark with a flashlight still gives you chills. More humorous than scary at this point, but a story or two are still as unsettling as they were to me as a child. Unfortunately, I do feel like a lot is lacking with Brett Helquist's artwork vs Stephen Gammell's. I think it takes away quite a bit from the imagery and atmosphere. It's cartoonish when these stories are far from that, even when the stories are funny. I understand that this serie</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8230014047221887199">Awesome when a book you read and reread as a child in the dark with a flashlight still gives you chills. More humorous than scary at this point, but a story or two are still as unsettling as they were to me as a child. Unfortunately, I do feel like a lot is lacking with Brett Helquist's artwork vs Stephen Gammell's. I think it takes away quite a bit from the imagery and atmosphere. It's cartoonish when these stories are far from that, even when the stories are funny. I understand that this series has been challenged and challenged over again, especially with the old -- more horrific -- illustrations, but that made it whole, really. This is a fraction of Scary Stories, and it's a good fraction, but a fraction nonetheless.</span>

          </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer45507811">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer232415551739996029">One of the most memorable series of books from my childhood. The stories in the books aren't particularly scary; some are humorous, some are eerie, some will give a kid chills...some are not even original to Mr. Schwartz, and are the sort of urban-legend stories you hear around the campfire growing up.<br /><br />No, what makes these spectacular books stand out as fine examples of kindertrauma is Stephen Gammell's most excellent illustrations.<br /><br />Some of them still give me heart palpitations, even as an adult.<br /><br />I</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText232415551739996029">One of the most memorable series of books from my childhood. The stories in the books aren't particularly scary; some are humorous, some are eerie, some will give a kid chills...some are not even original to Mr. Schwartz, and are the sort of urban-legend stories you hear around the campfire growing up.<br /><br />No, what makes these spectacular books stand out as fine examples of kindertrauma is Stephen Gammell's most excellent illustrations.<br /><br />Some of them still give me heart palpitations, even as an adult.<br /><br />I pull this series out to decorate my table every Halloween, and I can't wait to scare the pants off my kids with them (as soon as they're old enough). &gt;;)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1048777860">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1048777860" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5537068-katy-jane" class="left imgcol" title="Katy Jane "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1354423734p2/5537068.jpg" alt="Katy Jane " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1048777860?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 07, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5537068-katy-jane" class="user" title="Katy Jane ">Katy Jane </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/413110.More_Scary_Stories_to_Tell_in_the_Dark" title="Hardcover 9780397320820" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1048777860">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17480273477506365343">1. At 28, these are no where near as scary as when I was 8, 9, 10 years old. I would stay up at night thinking about these stories and freak myself out.<br />2. I am reading them again because this month is banned books month and this is a book that is challenged almost ever year. Reasons being: insensitivity, Satanism/occult, unsuited for age group, violence, religious viewpoint.<br />3. These being banned make little sense to me because they are a collection of folklore that have been around for forever.<br />4</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17480273477506365343">1. At 28, these are no where near as scary as when I was 8, 9, 10 years old. I would stay up at night thinking about these stories and freak myself out.<br />2. I am reading them again because this month is banned books month and this is a book that is challenged almost ever year. Reasons being: insensitivity, Satanism/occult, unsuited for age group, violence, religious viewpoint.<br />3. These being banned make little sense to me because they are a collection of folklore that have been around for forever.<br />4. Stephen Gammell's illustrations are what scare me the most. They are so disturbingly wonderful. I want a print for my house, actually. <br />5. Stories that stood out to me: The Brown Suit, The Bad News, The Dead Man's Hand, The Bed by the Window, Wonderful Sausage, Rings on Her Fingers, The Bride. I think most of these stayed in my mind because they could actually happen. The beginning of the book was about ghost stories but these other ones were stories with unexplained happening that could have actually taken place. Those are also the scary movies that frighten me the most. THE ONES WHO COULD ACTUALLY HAPPEN. <br />6. I enjoyed the annotations at the end of the book. They explained where some stories came from and the history behind them.<br />7. I can't wait to have children to read these to and introduce at sleep overs. And then clean up the pee when they wet themselves and dry the tears when they cry themselves to sleep.<br />8. My cat kept creeping me out while reading this. He got under the recliner and kept pawing me through the crack of the seat and then when I least expected it, jumped in my lap. Warning: remove pets from room when reading this book. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17480273477506365343">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_999174019">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/999174019" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6831741-g-b-lindsey" class="left imgcol" title="G.B. Lindsey"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442968767p2/6831741.jpg" alt="G.B. Lindsey" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/999174019?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 17, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6831741-g-b-lindsey" class="user" title="G.B. Lindsey">G.B. Lindsey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer999174019">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7109699224766569023">Wow, talk about trauma.<br /><br />One appalling day about two-odd years ago, my sister and I stood utterly frozen in the bookstore in a godawful hive-minded fury (i.e., what my sister defines not as angry but as "shangry plus") when we saw that they had dared to re-release this trilogy WITHOUT THE ORIGINAL STEPHEN GAMMELL ILLUSTRATIONS. Unspeakable is the rage that resulted, the high-pitched squeaks and the flailing that nearly knocked books from their shelves, and oh god, the SPUTTERING. We clung to each</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7109699224766569023">Wow, talk about trauma.<br /><br />One appalling day about two-odd years ago, my sister and I stood utterly frozen in the bookstore in a godawful hive-minded fury (i.e., what my sister defines not as angry but as "shangry plus") when we saw that they had dared to re-release this trilogy WITHOUT THE ORIGINAL STEPHEN GAMMELL ILLUSTRATIONS. Unspeakable is the rage that resulted, the high-pitched squeaks and the flailing that nearly knocked books from their shelves, and oh god, the SPUTTERING. We clung to each other and wept for the fate of unsuspecting newbies, innocently picking up this new release and never fated to understand the awesomeness that was these books.<br /><br />I still own my original copies of this trilogy. As in, covers sagging off, pages dog-eared to hell, half of Book 1 falling out of its binding, juice and tea and coffee stains on the pages depending on how old I was when I re-read (yes, re-read, as in ALL THE TIME, HOT DAMN, RE-READ THIS SUCKER BECAUSE IT'S HALLOWEEN OR A DARK AND STORMY NIGHT OR, YOU KNOW, TUESDAY) the books, my name written with the crooked grace of an 11-year-old on the inside of each cover. I still remember The Hearse Song and There Was a Man Who Lived in Leeds by heart. I knew them by heart before I rightly knew what they meant. The Wendigo introduced me to what remains THE scariest story I have ever come across, and damn it, did I remember that story for the next 20-and-counting years. I can shout ME-TIE-DOUGHTY-WALKER and rest assured of the answering screech LYNCHY-KINCHY-COLLY-MOLLY-DINGO-DINGO across the parking lot as another hapless member of my generation gathers up his or her dog and scrambles in the opposite direction, groceries sailing out of bags onto the pavement.<br /><br />No review will do justice to the amount of bone-deep delight I have experienced due to the existence of these books. If ever I mention these books to the friends of mine I have retained since my elementary school years, I invariably receive responses ranging from "OmigodHarold" to "Hey, remember that picture of the Thing?" to "KILL IT WITH FIRE, I CAN'T EVER EAT SAUSAGE AGAIN AND I STILL CHECK MY BACK SEAT WHENEVER I GET INTO MY CAR, GET AWAY FROM ME."<br /><br />For the record, I also check my back seat. ^_^ <br /><br />I flirted briefly with the notion of buying the one-book compendium with the original artwork but decided I enjoy the street cred of my three old busted-ass copies and I will never give them up, not even when they've fallen to pieces and my family stages an intervention because "Oh my gawd, Grete, can you please see reason, there are maggots in these." <br /><br />Alas, the joke's on them. They will have to pry them from my cold, dead fingers.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7109699224766569023">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11300247902441531197"> No matter how safe you think you are, something evil is always waiting for you! Scary stories is a horrifying book of short scary stories. My favorite short story was The Babysitter. It told the story of a babysitter who was watching 3 kids. She got a phone call at 9:00 from someone creepily laughing. The man called back every 30 minutes and at 10:30 he said he was going to come to them very soon. Being frightened the babysitter called the cops, then they told her that the man was calling from</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11300247902441531197"> No matter how safe you think you are, something evil is always waiting for you! Scary stories is a horrifying book of short scary stories. My favorite short story was The Babysitter. It told the story of a babysitter who was watching 3 kids. She got a phone call at 9:00 from someone creepily laughing. The man called back every 30 minutes and at 10:30 he said he was going to come to them very soon. Being frightened the babysitter called the cops, then they told her that the man was calling from upstairs. All of the sudden the upstairs door slowly crèches open!<br /> Scary stories was a chilling and very entertaining book. Even though. The stories weren't as scary as the first book they still creeped me out! The writing was very effective which made me scared. The book was still scary enough for me to want to read the 3rd one. I recommend this book to someone who wants to be chilled and creeped out but not having the effect of the first Scary Stories that made me want to look behind my shoulder every few seconds! <br /></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1408329767">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15967005697298149590">The authors purpose for writing this book is to entertain the child public with scary stories told down families for generations. Mr. Schwartz has wrote many books on scary stories and some of his stories are very convincing to the children who read them. Such as the Sasquatch, it is a story that many people think exist or existed at sometime. Schwartz wrote this to inform kids about these legends as entertainment and information.<br /><br />There isn't a real theme to this book except for scariness. I thin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15967005697298149590">The authors purpose for writing this book is to entertain the child public with scary stories told down families for generations. Mr. Schwartz has wrote many books on scary stories and some of his stories are very convincing to the children who read them. Such as the Sasquatch, it is a story that many people think exist or existed at sometime. Schwartz wrote this to inform kids about these legends as entertainment and information.<br /><br />There isn't a real theme to this book except for scariness. I think Mr. Schwartz made this book not intended for a lesson but a information giver such as one of his stories A Weird Blue Light. If he has a real theme it is extremely hidden.<br /><br />Mr. Schwartz writing style was narration, telling the story through a series of events that describe what happened. The reason his writing is narration is because he is explaining scary stories and how they happened or what they were about. I think narration is one of the best writing styles because they are more informing you than entertaining you as a book.<br /><br />My opinion on this book is that it could have been more clear it is very much unclear and hard to understand the authors exact point. The stories when understandable were quite entertaining. I would recommend this book to some of my friends that like scary movies/stories because of their interest in the genre of scary stories.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_893755199">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/893755199" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/128091-jenny" class="left imgcol" title="Jenny"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1420042826p2/128091.jpg" alt="Jenny" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/893755199?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 09, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/128091-jenny" class="user" title="Jenny">Jenny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1169067.More_Scary_Stories_To_Tell_In_The_Dark" title="Library Binding 9780808579953" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer893755199">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7262569224421120657">This series of books scared the crap out of me when I was a kid. I still vividly remember their exact place on the elementary school library shelf, and the feeling of dread I got when I took one down. As many other reviewers have noted, however, when reading these as an adult it's obvious that it isn't the stories that are scary but the art. The stories hardly even count as stories--most are barely more than slightly spooky anecdotes--but the art is still unsettling, twenty-some years after I la</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7262569224421120657">This series of books scared the crap out of me when I was a kid. I still vividly remember their exact place on the elementary school library shelf, and the feeling of dread I got when I took one down. As many other reviewers have noted, however, when reading these as an adult it's obvious that it isn't the stories that are scary but the art. The stories hardly even count as stories--most are barely more than slightly spooky anecdotes--but the art is still unsettling, twenty-some years after I last looked at it.<br /><br />I like how well-documented the stories are, though, and it's neat to have a compendium like this of long-told scary tales. Still, it's Stephen Gammell's art that makes these books worth seeking out. I was ecstatic to find this copy at this year's library sale, even though it doesn't have the original cover that I remember so well. The art is still pure Gammell, though, and not the cleaned-up Brett Helquist version that came out in 2011 for the series' 30th anniversary. Pretty lame gift, if you ask me. Although I like Helquist's work in the Lemony Snicket books, replacing Gammell's work in Scary Stories with anything else is just blasphemy. This alteration makes me all the more excited to seek out the other two original books, though, and hopefully one day compile a whole set with the original covers.<br /><br />Seriously, though, the nightmare-inducing power of the images in this book cannot be overestimated. Open it at your own risk. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7262569224421120657">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2mCUOIzlUQeAiufv0Csuq4mG50UcAadoJSmJk38wKfm/tKvrfjdF/QxSk1SuSsgZwHEkXFXc4MJPIIwBs6XfvA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/13728.Alvin_Schwartz">About Alvin Schwartz</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer13949624637673068260">Alvin Schwartz was the author of more than fifty books dedicated to and dealing with topics such as folklore and word play, many of which were intended for young readers. He is often confused with another Alvin Schwartz, who wrote Superman and Batman daily comics strips and a novel titled The Blowtop.</span>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/13728.Alvin_Schwartz" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Alvin Schwartz...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
